Tab 10 Post Office Insurance Financial Conduct Authority Dual Pricing Change Impact

POST OFFICE LIMITED
RISK & COMPLIANCE COMMITTEE REPORT

Title: Financial Conduct Authority pricing I meeting pate: I 12 November 2020
rules changes

muthar Ed Dutton, Post Office Insurance Sponsor: Owen Woodley, Chief Commercial
Managing Director Officer

Input Sought: Noting

The Committee is asked to note that:

- the Financial Conduct Authority (FCA) recently announced proposals to prohibit ‘Price
Walking’ (competitive new business prices followed by renewal prices increasing during
contract) in Motor and Home Insurance, along with changes to Product Governance and
reporting of value metrics; and

- the insurance team have begun to mobilise a programme, overseen by a Post Office
Insurance (POI) Board committee, to respond effectively,

for onward submissions to the Audit, Risk & Compliance Committee (ARC).

Previous Governance Oversight
e POI Board discussions

Report

Background

1. The FCA have produced their Final Report on General Insurance Pricing Practices 18/1.3

2. They have been reviewing pricing differentials within household and motor insurance for
some time. Predominantly, their review work has focused on differentials between new
and existing customers.

3. Over time, customers who stick with their insurer can see their premiums increase
significantly compared to customers who shop around. This practice is known as price
walking.

4. Their work within this area is aligned to a wider Competition and Markets Authority (CMA)
review which focuses on pricing in several market areas including general insurance and
broadband.

5. The FCA had already concluded that there is significant detriment within the market,
highlighting that overall, six million customers were being overcharged for their motor and
household insurance, with this overcharging totalling some £1.2bn.

6. There is some evidence that the impact of price walking is felt disproportionally by
vulnerable customers and older customers.

The Proposed Remedies

7. The core solution proposed by the FCA is that new and renewing customers should pay
the same price. This will not prevent the provision by firms of differing prices to customer
where the firm operates via different brands and channels.

8. This will require significant changes to pricing models across the industry.

Confidential

Post Office Limited - Risk and Compliance Committee-12/11/20 133 of 226

POL-BSFF-0238386_0132
POL00423571
POL00423571

Tab 10 Post Office Insu

nce Financial Conduct Authority Dual Pricing Change Impact

@

9. There will be anti-avoidance measures in place to prevent firms from avoiding the intent
of the rules. These will be developed over the coming months.

10. Additionally, Firms will also need more formal processes for assessing products and the
FCA will be implementing piloted proposals on reporting value measures.

11. Note that these additional rules apply across GI and not to just household and motor
business.

12. Extensive MI reporting on compliance with the new pricing regime will also be required.

13. The FCA notes it will police markets vigorously and will be looking to implement attestation
and other requirements as part of this policing process.

14. Under SMCR, it will require firms to be clear on pricing accountability and to focus on fair
value, noting that the Boards of regulated firms should have a clear line of sight on pricing
practices.

Timin

15. The FCA is now consulting on these proposals.

16. The deadline for consultations on the paper is 25 January 2021.

17. The FCA then proposes to produce final rules and guidance in the second quarter of the

2021 calendar year, with an expected launch date within 4-6 months of that (although
the market is unconvinced that is realistic).

Potential Impact

18. Whilst the basic principles of the change are straightforward, there are a large number of
technical uncertainties around interpretation. Indeed, whilst the FCA have attended
various forums to explain their thoughts to Industry Bodies, it is apparent that conflicting
explanations or guidance on specific technical points have been given.

19. Ultimately, whilst the overall market value may reduce slightly, the basic impact will be
that value shifts from renewing policies, where margins will reduce, to new business
policies, where margins will be significantly higher than now.

20. Asaresult, the impact appears likely to differ very significantly depending on the size and
scale of existing business.

21. This could be:

© companies that have very significant back books of business where, if they want to
sell new business, their renewal prices will have to fall. Or,

o where large businesses are very complex — the are market comments regarding how
many different sets of prices very large consolidated firms like Aviva have in the
market - becoming compliant (in terms of governance, reporting AND pricing) could
be very complicated, difficult and expensive.

22. POI has recorded a risk that we respond poorly or too slowly - i.e. our pricing model
response is mis-judged and our commercial outcomes compared to the current outlook
are degraded, or that we are not ready to fulfil the regulatory requirements in terms of
our pricing, our governance or the new reporting.

23. However, having (until recently) shrunk our Motor and Home books over recent years,
there is the potential for this to be a material opportunity for POI, assuming we can
continue to write significant New Business volumes (at higher prices and positive margins)
relative to our current (small) mature book size.

Confidential

134 of 226 Post Office Limited - Risk and Compliance Committee-12/11/20

POL-BSFF-0238386_0133

je Impact

@

Activity underway within POI to achieve compliance

Tab 10 Post Office Insurance Financial Conduct Authority Dual Pricing C

24. Given the technical uncertainties, we are working directly with the ABI and BIBA to gain
greater clarity from the FCA, and to influence their responses to the FCA consultation
paper.

25. We are also already heavily engaged with our main partners (Ageas for Home Insurance
and BGL for Motor Insurance), as we have significant dependencies on each other to
operate compliantly in the future and to maximise the opportunity/mitigate any risk.

26. POI board has been very focussed on this change in market practice and is overseeing our
response via a Board oversight committee, led by a NED.

27. Weare in the process of mobilising a focussed change programme to ensure success.

28. The initial activity underway is to generate a more detailed impact assessment of the rules
on a set of workstreams, currently including technical pricing, MI and reporting,
underwriting partners, finance, governance.

29. This initial discovery phase will inform a more detailed programme scope, deliverables and
plan, and resource requirements.

30. Significant change investment and human resources will be required, and specialist
resource may be required for some elements.

31. We are reviewing some initial output of this phase for a couple of workstreams on Friday
13%" November with the POI Board Oversight Committee, as well as continuing to inform
progress on mobilisation of the programme.

32. The programme will follow POL change procedures, as well as be overseen by the POI
board, and we will enter the change governance process imminently.

Tab 11 Committee Terms of Reference

@

POST OFFICE LIMITED
RISK & COMPLIANCE COMMITTEE REPORT

Risk & Compliance Committee

Title: Meeting Date: I 12" November 2020
Terms of Reference

muthar Rebecca Whibley, Senior Assistant Sponsor: Veronica Branton, Group
Company Secretary Company Secretary

Input Sought: Discussion & Decision

The Risk & Compliance Committee (RCC) are asked to review and discuss the draft RCC Terms
of Reference, including, particularly, the membership of the RCC in light of the recent
organisational design changes and then approve the RCC Terms of Reference, subject to any
amendments as agreed by the RCC during its discussions for onward submission to the Group
Executive (GE).

Executive Summary

Following the adoption of the new Articles of Association for the Group in April 2020, the
Company Secretariat reviewed the Group Governance Framework and redrafted the Matters
Reserved to the Board and Committee Terms of Reference for all Group Companies. These
revised documents were adopted by the relevant Group Companies between April and June
2020. As a result the RCC Terms of Reference required review to align with these changes.
Further, the RCC Terms of Reference have not been reviewed since 2016. It is good governance
for all committees at Board and Executive level to have terms of reference and for these to be
reviewed annually.

As such, the RCC Terms of Reference have been reviewed to align with the new Governance
Framework, current practice and to reflect the agreed Terms of Reference structure for the
Group.

Given the recent organisational changes, it is understood that this will affect the membership
of the RCC and therefore the RCC is asked to discuss and propose the future membership of
the Committee as appropriate. The Committee is then asked to approve the Terms of
Reference, subject to any amendments agreed, for onward submission to the GE, who will be
asked to review and approved the Terms of Reference at its meeting in December 2020.

Post Office Limited
(“the Company”)
Terms of Reference of Risk and Compliance Committee

The Risk and Compliance Committee (RCC) is a standing committee of the Group
Executive (GE). Its authority is subject to the powers and duties of the Company
Board, as set out in the Articles of Association and the Framework Document.

A. Purpose
1. The purpose of the RCC is to support the GE in fulfilling their responsibilities
in the effective oversight of risk management, internal control and
assurance, and compliance in the Group.
B. Duties and Responsibilities
2. The RCC shall review and approve for recommendation (where
applicable) to the Audit, Risk & Compliance Committee all papers and
decisions prior to submission to the Audit, Risk and Compliance Committee.
3. The RCC shall also:
Risk Management Framework
i. Review the effectiveness of the risk management framework and
maintain oversight of the development and implementation of the

components of the risk management framework;

. Monitor Maintain-eversight-of the current risk exposures of Post Office
Group and advise on future risk strategy;

iii, Review the identification and effective management of current key

risks and identified mitigating actions and regular reviews of emerging
risks.;

iv. Consider-and-Rreview areas of risk, which should include,but-is-not
limited-to,-sufficient-coverage-of enterprise and linked intermediate
risks.?

Limited (Post Office Insurance) and Payzone Bill Payments Limited.

Tab 12 Deepdive: Multiple Partner Failure

POST OFFICE LIMITED
RISK & COMPLIANCE COMMITTEE REPORT

Multiple partner financial stability

Title: update Meeting Date: I 12 November 2020
7 Karl Oliver, Head of Commercial . Amanda Jones, Group Retail and
actives Partnerships Spurenars Franchise Network Director

Input Sought: Note

The Committee is asked to note the partner financial stability update for onward submission
to the Audit, Risk & Compliance Committee (ARC).

Previous Governance Oversight
ARC papers Sept’19 and Mar’20.

Executive Summary

1. Inthe ARC meeting Sept’19, we shared a paper outlining how we track the financial stability
of our largest partners and followed-up with a contingency plan in ARC March’20 which set
out how we would maintain PO services in the event of the closure of a large number of
PO's as a result of Partner financial collapse. This paper provides an update on the financial
tracking of the partners incorporating the known marketplace impact of covid.

2. Of our 6 major partners, 4 are classed as ‘Green’ (low risk) using our financial stability
measures. We do have concerns around McColls and WHS and both are currently classed
as ‘Amber’ (medium risk).

3. Appendix 2 shows key financial highlights for McColls and WHS. For McColls it highlights
slight improvements for cash and debt, with share price decline remaining a concern. For
WHSmiths it highlights the forecast loss of £70-75m but currently with good access to
cash/credit. Neither status has been adjusted and both will continue to be tracked closely
as AMBER.

4. Both businesses have been under considerable cost pressures for some time and the impact
of Covid has only served to exacerbate this. Our intention has been to work closely with
both McColls and WHS to agree pragmatic ways to help them move to a more sustainable
estate/model and therefore maintain PO services for customers.

5. As was highlighted in the report to ARC in September last year, we have limited access to
Analyst/Broker insights to understand the underlying financial health of some of our largest
partners. At the time we explored subscription to Thomson Reuters platform that provided
additional financial KPIs but this was discounted as it added ‘data’ rather than insight.

6. Our recommendation is that we re-look at options within a budget envelope of no more

than £30k. Options to be reviewed to include retaining access to an analyst and utilisation
of an ‘insight/knowledge marketplace’ (e.g. Gerson Lehman Group, GLG model).

7. Since we last reviewed the financial tracking and operational plans with RCC/ARC the
partner planning has informed the ‘early days’ covid response and worked well to accelerate
our set-up. We have taken the improved reporting and prioritisation from the covid planning
to strengthen the partner plan>

Questions addressed

8. How do we track the financial stability of our strategic partners?
9. What is the current financial status for each of our strategic partners?
10. What is POL doing to support/mitigate risk with the AMBER Partners?

Report
How do we track the financial stability of our strategic partners?

11. Following engagement with Risk, BEIS and finance the ‘financial resilience tracker’ was
established in P1, 2019 to formally review finances and significant account activity for our
6 largest partners. The financial measures where appropriate mirror those tracked by BEIS
and are reviewed by period looking for any indication of distress.

External distress signals would include profit warnings; cash constrained - low liquidity
headroom; prospective covenant breaches; Poor financial ratios particularly gearing,
operating margin, ROI/ROA; credit status downgrade; share price underperformance;
failed refinancing and/or new management team.

12. We currently track share price and trend, Experian ratings, key ratios (net debt vs EBITDA,
total debt vs equity and interest payment cover) and formal announcements from the
partner to create a RAG rating for each partner. Tracking of industry media & social feeds
and insight gained from relationships is included under internal measures, with any
significant events fed back through Retail Director updates. The P6, 2020 financial tracker
is included in Appendix 1.

Tab 12 Deepdive: Multiple Partner Failure

17. McColls (status: AMBER)

e McColls published their interim results in July’20, with overall flat trading figures the
share price following an initially positive response has dropped 38% in the last 3 months
and although debt has reduced by c.£8m it remains high

e  LFL trading was +8.3% (McColls interim results) with trading during covid period
+c.20% and c.+4% vs Convenience sector through Mar-May (Neilson)

¢ McColls have continued their estate review with a net PO reduction of 5 sites and a
further 84 (15 closures and 69 to be sold) will be disposed of as part of this programme

e McColls PO performance recovered quickly benefitting from local shopping, initial drop
in April was -20% YoY and average PO trading for the last 3 months of +3.5% YoY

18. WHS (status: AMBER)

e WHS published interim results in May’20 and a further trading update in Aug’20 in
response to the covid impact on both their high street and travel businesses

e WHS share price has dropped by 49% following the covid outbreak and they moved
quickly raise funds through a share placing and to secure access to enough credit to
cover an extended period of limited trading (c.£400m at May 20, WHS accounts)

e We have 7 x PO resignations from WHS where they have failed to reach agreement on
new terms with landlords

e PO performance has recovered from -63% YoY in April to -25% YoY for the last 3 months
but lockdown 2 is likely to negatively impact as WHS sites are ‘town centre’ sites

What is POL doing to support/mitigate risk with the AMBER Partners?

19. McColls

e We have maintained our controls and contingency plan for a McColls failure (as covered
in Mar’20) but are working closely with them on the rationalisation of their estate as
they continue the transition from ‘Newsagents’ to ‘convenience operators’

« They have shared the detailed store disposal plan and how this impacts the operation
of POs in their estate. Their estate review will reduce their PO sites by 134 sites, from
607 to 473 (with c.50 completed so far). This 134 site reduction will be achieved through
the closure of 52 sites (37 closed) and sale of 82 sites (13 sold). They are reducing their
overall retail estate by c.350 sites over the same period.

e The remaining 15 sites for closure all have closure dates in this financial year. McColls
have served full notice on all sites and have extended past official closure dates to assist
when we have temporary operators in place (4 stores re-opened with temporary
Postmaster).

e We have proactively advertised all the ‘for sale’ sites through our ‘Run a Post Office’
website to help McColls find buyers, with 13 now sold; 50 are ‘under offer’ and the final
19 remain advertised.

« We continue to support McColl’s Post Office with operational advice, resource mapping
and training of additional support staff for covid impacted stores.

+ Total revenue decreased by 1.0% to £605m in IH20, primarily reflecting store
closures during this period and the temporary withdrawal of scratch cards
+ This was however offset by stronger demand observed in the groceries
market driven by the Covid-19 outbreak, particularly for food and alcohol

top-up purchases to planned lower-margin take home products, as well as
multi-buys and value items

product areas

(2019: £89.7m)

POST OFFICE LIMITED
RISK & COMPLIANCE COMMITTEE REPORT

Transformation Office Change
Update 2020

Saira Burwood, Head of SPO &
Author: Joanne Welch, Change Risk & Sponsor:
Assurance Manager

Title: Meeting Date: I 12 November 2020

Dan Zinner, Group Chief Strategy
and Transformation Officer

Input Sought: Noting

The Committee is asked to note an update on improvements implemented to better manage
Change, ensure the effective delivery of Change, and to approve further adoption and continued
improvement, for onward submission to the Audit, Risk & Compliance Committee (ARC).

Previous Governance Oversight
e ARC update on 13th September 2019
e Risk & Compliance Committee (RCC) update on 7th November 2019
e Internal Audit report dated 4th May 2020

Executive Summary

At the September 2019 ARC meeting, an update was provided on the current short-term focus
of the Chief Transformation Officer (CTO) and the centralisation of the Change function. The
CTO’s plan was focused on immediate improvement in the oversight and delivery of Change
(‘doing things right’) not on the Strategy (‘doing the right things’). It concentrated on three
areas: People, Process and Perception.

Since then a significant amount of work has taken place and the POL Change organisation has
evolved into a centralised, collaborative and effective function with clear accountabilities and
management. Capable and competent resources are on appropriately configured teams, the
quality of support across Change has increased, oversight has been enhanced through better
tooling, new rhythms and reports to provide transparency, and governance processes and
controls have been further improved and embedded to drive consistency.

To further support delivery of the CTO plan, a new “Change Control Framework” (CCF) was
developed. The CCF was deployed formally to the Change Community and wider Business in
February 2020 and has subsequently been captured for onward management within Archer
GRC tool. In July 2020, Internal Audit noted that that there was already a noticeable
improvement in the consistency and effectiveness of controls operation at programme level.
More information on the CCF can be found in the Reading Room.

Acontinuous improvement programme is in place and opportunities are identified and delivered
around our current processes, principles, artefacts, tooling and adoption. Our ongoing learnings
from post-implementation reviews, health checks, 1st/2nd line assurance and self-identified
gaps and weaknesses through our CCF also continue to drive improvements across Change.

While a lot of progress has been made, there’s still more to do. Focus over the last year has
been on the Change Community, and further work is now required to bring management along
on the overall Change vision and journey. This includes broadening stakeholder understanding
of, and conviction for, how ‘Change works’ at the Post Office to make the process more efficient,
and assisting the GE to role model appropriate behaviours of change management, including

i,

Questions addressed

1. I What changes have been implemented across Transformation since the last ARC update?
2. How effective is the CCF in mitigating & managing Change Risks?
3. What lessons have been learnt and what areas will be focused on next?

Report

ie changes have been implemented across Transformation since the last ARC

update?

rhe September 2019, the CTO set out to embed Change processes and ways of working
through consistency, clarification and communication. Initial efforts focused on the Change
community and increasing understanding on how to consistently manage and resource a
project for delivery, before further engaging the overall business on Change. Three key
areas were focussed on (People, Process and Perception) and the following section outlines
what has been implemented so far in each of these areas.

2. Regarding the key deliverables relating to People, 3 sub-themes were identified:
a. Structure Change teams that are fit for purpose and leverage current resources to
ensure people are working within their scope and ability

i. Project Delivery Team manager in place since November 2019 to directly line
manage, develop and track (against performance metrics and project data
quality metrics) all Project/Programme Manager (PM), Business Analyst (BA) and
Project Management Office (PMO) resources, and ensure appropriate alignment
of resources to projects based on their scope and ability, and the project needs.

ii. Central cross-charging through our ServiceNow tool of BAU resources who work
on projects is now in place (e.g. SME, Product Owner, Solution Architect, lawyers)
which ensures better forward and historical visibility of all project costs and
appropriate accounting. In September, 60 BAU resources were cross-charged.

b. Increase the number of capable and affordable Change resources, not necessarily total
resources

i. We have rebalanced the Change Delivery Skills Group resource split from 47%
employees (FTE and FTC) on 31% August 2019 to 53% employees on 31%t August
2020 to lower overall costs, with the remainder filled by contractors.

ii. 100% of Skills Group pool resources undergo an induction, within 1 month of
joining Change, on the Change Excellence Framework and the 8 PM minimum
standards on which they must comply. We have completed 53 inductions in the
last 12 months. A BA framework has also been developed and will be embedded
in Q3. Both frameworks include compliance metrics.

c. Clearly communicate the value of the centralised Change support team structure and
roles and constantly ensure this is fit for purpose and cost

Tab 13 Deepdive: Change/Transformation Update

@

i. The centralised SPO function had 14 FTEs in August 2019 and following the recent
restructure in August 2020 now has 9.5 FTEs with an overall cost saving of 30%.
While the number of Change projects within has not reduced significantly,
efficiencies were made due to better IT tooling, focus on improved data quality
and more standardisation across processes. Focus is now on governance,
resources, assurance/oversight and further tooling improvements.

ii. Further FTE reductions were made with a ‘Portfolio of Change’ restructure from
8 portfolios in August 2019, down to 5 portfolios, removing 6 FTEs with an
annualised saving of over 40%.

3. Key deliverables relating to Process:
a. Operationalise Change routines and rhythms, ensuring consistency and speed across
the business
i. ServiceNow has been embedded and adopted and is used as our ‘single source
of truth’ for all project data. It is widely used to produce a variety of dashboards
and reports on all aspects of Change delivery including the monthly UKGI Change
update report, Portfolio performance metrics, project costs & benefits, Change
data quality, resource allocation etc. to drive key decisions by senior
management and support PMs in successful project delivery. We have 355 risks
and 305 milestones against 92 listed projects today versus 555 risks (included
duplications and poor data) and 55 milestones against 132 listed projects in
October 2019. (See Appendix 1 - Example of weekly project metrics dashboard)
b. Embed the Governance process and tools, with improved efficiency, effectiveness and
agility

i. To reduced administration and increase efficiencies the SPO has agreed and
documented a number of exceptional processes for activities which do not suit
the standard CEF lifecycle yet still require some light touch governance and
oversight (i.e. IT Risk & Resilience, Property CapEx, small BF2 client funded
projects, and NDA activities). These are inline with our Change Policy and the

CCF to ensure minimum control standards are reflected.

ii. The capture and sharing of project lessons learnt plays a key role in ensuring we
learn from our mistakes. The Change community and key stakeholders receive
a regular overview of key themes being seen in Post-Implementation Reviews
and Project Health Checks (See Appendix 2 - Key PIR Themes Report) and
appropriate remediation plans and controls improvements are agreed to further
strengthen our overall governance processes and CCF.

iii. The Business Readiness Assurance (BRA) process has been enhanced to ensure
earlier stakeholder engagement. New projects attend the Gating forum at project
outset to ensure their impacted stakeholders are aware of issues and have been
involved in developing mitigation plans. 100% (20) Projects received approval
first time in Q2 2020 versus Q2 2019 where 12 projects went through gating with
only 25% (3) approved first time and 58% (7) conditionally approved.

Tab 13 Deepdive: Change/Transformation Update

@

iv. Following CCF assessemnt, more robust processes and controls have been
implemented including reducing spend tolerance (from 10% to 2%) which
prevents any project from raising a Purchase Order or committing spend more
than 2% above their approved budget.

4. Key deliverables relating to Perception:

a. Foster understanding, conviction and alignment within the Change community on how
the PO “does Change,” which includes training and constant “on the job” practice in
new ways of working

i. More frequent communications are in place to build knowledge and engagement
e.g. a weekly newsletter, the All Hands Change monthly meeting, Communities
of Practice.

b. Bring management along on the overall change vision and journey

i. The GE/Investment committee have requested more transparency and a desire
to see that we are delivering change consistently and learning from our mistakes,
but there is still more work to do here in order to support the GE in role modelling
appropriate behaviours of change management including decisiveness and
consequence management.

5. This is all underpinned by the CCF which identifies all Change risks, control procedures and
remediation. The CCF has promoted a cultural shift, increasing awareness that there are
risks to be managed and the importance of adherence to our controls and processes. It has
driven accountability across Change with risk and control owners identified, and supported
enhanced oversight and assurance of change. Work is now underway to fully operationalise
the CCF with periodic assessment on the risks and controls.

How effective is the CCF in mitigating & managing Change Risks?

6. The CCF was developed with support from Internal audit in Q3 2019, deployed to the change
community in February 2020 and loaded into the Archer tool in Q2 2020 along with the
Change Risks (Enterprise, Intermediate and Local risk register risks). The CCF currently
holds 53 controls and includes all the checks, challenges, and reports to enable projects to
deliver on time, on budget, to the required quality to enable benefits to be realised. These
activities are in place at governance, portfolio and project levels throughout the project life
cycle until project benefits are transferred to business areas to track to fruition. (See
Appendix 3 for a summary of the CCF)

7. Control procedures have been strengthened by defining the activities undertaken, detailing
the type of control, its design, ownership and its frequency of operation. The relationship
between each control procedures and the risk it helps to mitigate/manage has been linked
within Archer and a standard operating procedure defining how SPO Risks and Controls
should be identified, assessed, tested, remediated and reported has been issued.

8. The controls were tested in January and September 2020 with overall control effectiveness
levels increasing by 51%. (see Appendix 4, fig.1-4) The testing cycle for each control has

evidence. A thematic assessment of 1* line Portfolio Assurance has been completed with a

9. Periodically Change risks residual scores will be re-evaluated based on environmental factors
and any improvements made to the control. The overall effectiveness of Risk Controls will
be re-assessed by the risk owners as remediation plans complete. Any additional
remediations will be captured at this time.

What lessons have been learnt and what will focus be on next?

10.This year 15 PIRs, 6 Project Deep dives and 1 Thematic review has been completed resulting
in 50 improvement recommendations. One common theme identified across these reviews
has been inaccurate benefits, either due to over estimation, erosion due to changes in
schedule or an inaccurate initial cost forecast. These recommendations have resulted in
updates to governance forum TORs, benefit & cost forecasting roles and responsibilities and
supporting RACI being developed, and additional business training planned for Q3.

1

in

.Business change management practices and suppliers’ learnings have also been highlighted
and are shared regularly with the wider change community via the PM Communities of
Practice. A detailed mapping of recommendations against SPO control area can be seen in
Appendix 4 - SPO Controls Assessment fig. 5-8.

12.The lessons learnt repository within ServiceNow has been embedded, with all projects
recording lessons throughout their lifecycle. There are currently 157 lessons logged. This
repository is searchable and is being used by project managers to identify lessons at project
initiation to help them succeed in areas where others have fallen foul.

13.In H2 we plan to focus on the wider business to improve their understanding on how ‘Change
works’ at the Post office and communicate our overall Change vision. This includes senior
management and the leadership teams (including the GE) and is particularly important and
timely following organisational changes. These session will refresh and reeducate Business
Sponsors of Change on our processes, controls and the importance of their role within
Change in particular, their accountabilities for benefit realisation throughout a project. This
will be supported by a quarterly Change communication to the wider busineses informing
them of latest updates and changes.

Next Steps & Timelines

We can return to the ARC in May 2021 to provide an update on the areas of focus identified
above if desired.

POST OFFICE LIMITED
RISK & COMPLIANCE COMMITTEE REPORT

Payzone Bill Payments Limited Risk
Update Report

Michelle Embrey, Quality & Risk
Author: Manager & Neil Davey, Operations I Sponsor:
Director

Title: Meeting Date: I 12" November 2020 I

Payments Managing Director

Andrew Goddard, Payzone Bill I

Input Sought: Noting

The Committee is asked to note the update on the previous Payzone Risk report last presented
to the Risk & Compliance Committee (RCC) and Audit, Risk & Compliance Committee (ARC) in
January 2020, for onward submission to the ARC.

Previous Governance Oversight

This is an action from the previous ARC meeting.

Executive Summary

In the January 2020 risk report, Payzone presented 5 significant risks. 4 of these risks had a
risk score of 12 and above, with the remaining risk of Brexit being an unpredictable event,
qualifying as a ‘Black Swan’ through its potential to become significant.

Since January, we mitigated the 3 most significant risks of Terminal Communication Issues,
GDPR Requirements and Policies & Operating Standards, and also improved and matured the
management of the risk framework across the operation of the business.

As a consequence of the Covid-19 pandemic, 4 new significant risks have been determined;
the commercial impact on Payzone’s clients, poor trading conditions, the dependency on 3"4
Parties, and the impact on retailer credit performance. We have been able to limit these new
risks to a score of 12 respectively, via a series of management controls and reporting.

The remaining risk from January is the ability for Payzone to deliver forecast revenues vs its
original plan. Given the impacts of the recent pandemic this risk has increased from a score of
15 to 20 to become our number 1 risk.

This paper details what steps Payzone has taken to improve managing risk and the movements
in our significant risks.

Tab 14 Payzone Risk Report

@

. What is the status of Payzone’s risk framework and what are the current key risks?
. What is the approach to risk appetite and key risk indicators?

Questions addressed
1
2
Report

1. Throughout 2020, Payzone has invested time and resources on its people, teams, and
processes to improve the way it manages risk and improves the risk culture:

a. Risk Review Meetings: A risk pack is generated monthly and submitted to
Payzone's senior management team for review and discussed during the monthly
risk review meetings. The risk owners are challenged on the appropriate
mitigating actions that are being taken to ensure the suitability to achieve the
target risk scores.

b. Risk Structure: A risk structure has been implemented which has identified the
main risk within Payzone (ability for Payzone to deliver the 5-year plan) and
promoted to an intermediate risk within the Post Office’s Archer risk management
system. A diagram has been included in Appendix 1 to illustrate the structure.

c. Risk Awareness: Risk awareness and the role of the risk team has been
presented to the wider Payzone business via a business update. There has been
separate participation in the weekly team meetings in Retail, Operation and
Commercial so individuals can assess and take responsibilities in identifying and
mitigating risks in their jobs and teams.

d. Rapid Response Team: Payzone set up a rapid response team through the initial
stage of the Covid 19 pandemic and we also participated as part of the Post Office
Rapid response team. We helped mitigate a risk in the Post Office Current Account
contact centre and their service levels by setting up a separate virtual contact
centre using Post Office employees self-isolating.

e. Process Improvements: In 2020, Payzone have matured in continually
improving processes to offset risk, with examples in sections 3 and 4 of this paper.
Payzone have also set up their own Change Approval Board and Project Review
Board. The Change Board has a various number of pre-checks and conversations
with key stakeholders to identify risks prior to a change being presented to the
Board for approval. Any risks to the delivery of business change and projects are
covered in subsequent Change Approval and Project Review Boards.

f. Post Office Risk Reporting: On a monthly basis, an update of the significant
risks are reported to Payzone’s Risk business partner within the Post Office risk
team. This is then consolidated amongst other group risks on the Archer risk
management system. This helps us identify if we need any support or resource
in managing risk and leveraging if other areas of the business are having similar
risks and sharing mitigation practices.

g. Alignment on Group Policies: The Post Office Limited draft policies are now
being reviewed by the Payzone Quality and Risk manager, for feedback prior to
final submission. This allows Payzone to operate within the policy of the group and
understand if any variations to that policy will be required. This has been 14
completed as part of a wider project to adopt or align the policies within Payzone
to the Post Office group policies.

The progress made against the key risks is summarised in Figure 1 with the details
outlined in sections 2 & 3 below.

Key Risks

2. January 2020 Mitigated Risks

a. Terminal Communication Issue: In January 2020, the terminal
communication issue was the highest risk with a risk score of 20. The
mitigations included several IT software releases to improve the communication
issue during spring 2020. This has been reflected in a reduction of inbound calls
to the Helpdesk regarding terminal communication from 20% down to 4%.
Further development has been completed which will enable the ability to
complete pre-payment gas transactions on a single device. Asa result, the risk
score has been reduced to from 20 to 6.

b. GDPR Requirements: Work has been ongoing in conjunction with the Post
Office Data Protection team to improve the governance surrounding data
protection within Payzone. A data protection process has been implemented
which includes data breach reporting and subject access requests. A weekly
progress meeting between Post Office data protection and Payzone’s Quality and
Risk Manager has been set up to provide support and ensure progress of
activities. Training material is being created to roll out to all Payzone employees
by Q4 2020/21. The actions implemented have reduced the risk score from 16
to a to a target score of a 4.

c. POL Policies and Operating Standards: A project has been set up to align
Payzone with the Post Office’s key group policies. This proposal was presented
to the Sept 2020 PZBP board with the objective to review 2 policies per month
until FY Q4. It is the intention that the Post Office key group policies will be
adopted where possible. If there are material differences, then variations will
be created. The risk score has reduced from 16 to 6.

d. Forecast Revenues and Brexit: These risks remain and are discussed in detail
in section 4 of this report.

3. Current Significant Risks

a. Intermediate Risk - the ability for Payzone to deliver the 5 yr plan risk
score 20 (5:4)
This risk has been promoted to become the intermediate risk at group level. The
5-year plan on revenue and cost lines has been re-forecasted as a response to
the changing priorities due to the demands on the business from the Covid-19 14
pandemic. At this stage, we continue to monitor the changes in customer buying
behaviour (cash to digital) and the requirements / desire of clients to enter into
exclusive contracts as well as plans to migrate to digital payments. To date, we
are not seeing evidence of this and in fact, the engagement with clients is more

3
Confidential

162 of 226 Post Office Limited - Risk and Compliance Committee-12/11/20

POL-BSFF-0238386_0161
POL00423571
POL00423571

Tab 14 Payzone Risk Report

@

positive and we have advanced dialogue with clients (e.g. e-On, Allpay) and
retailers (e.g. Tesco & Coop) to migrate transaction volume to the Post Office
and Payzone networks.

b. Poor trading conditions in the current pandemic (risk score 12)
The lockdown in Q1 had a initial downward impact on the bill payment trading
conditions with us performing 20% lower against the original budget for the
quarter, due to the elderly and high risk shielding at home and our clients
working with customers to help them pay their bills through non cash methods
or offering free credit and payment holidays. We have seen positive recovery
during Q2 with both Energy and Resellers returning to perform -10% against
budget and parcels have performed +20% YoY, but transport continues to
struggle due to the fear of using public transport and working from home.
However, our digital transport solution places in a good position as post-Covid
conversion from cash to smart card will be prevalent. We have aided our
recovery by signing new Energy clients in Bright and Jersey and driven new
volume from eOn, EDF and via our platform partners, Siemens and Itron who
prefer to deal with us over competitors. We will drive additional future revenue
from a planned exclusive relationship with eOn on smart and from new deals
with Allpay and Capita.

c. The impact of the Covid-19 pandemic on clients (risk score 12)
We are starting to see some of the smaller Energy companies struggle and fail
due to bad debt and a lack of contingency in their balance sheets. Their
customers however are being absorbed by the big 6 suppliers and we have seen
100,000 new customers added to BG’s customer base (Robin Hood Energy)
which will drive volume to our branch and store network in Q4. The transport
industry is in disarray and largely propped up by the government since late
spring, which will continue until people can travel freely. Parcel companies are
thriving due to an uplift in online shopping and this will continue for the long
term, benefitting Payzone via relations with HubBox (start up operator). We are
aligned with PUDO strategy work to determine the potential to leverage the
Payzone network to support the POL PUDO aspirations.

d. The long-term impact of the pandemic on finances (risk score 12)
The current situation is highly changeable with the unknown impact due to the
sporadic shifts in local lockdowns around the country. The actions completed
within the credit management function has resulted in a reduction in retailer
debt to below the levels seen pre-pandemic. The pre-pandemic levels of failed
direct debit were at a level of 1.5% (£182k) per week and a collection rate of
95.5% (£174k). This has reduced to a level of only 0.5% for failed direct debits
and a collection rate of 100%. These exceptional levels have been achieved by
a combination of activities including improvements to the collection process to
collaborate with retailers that fail direct debits, improvements in the quality of
new retailers which has been aided with the implementation of a defined credit
policy, publicising card payments as well as cash payments. The aged debt
levels have also decreased which has been facilitated by a change to how the 14
inbound calls are processed. These calls are now routed to the Helpdesk which
has resulted in the credit team’s ability to dedicate more time to resolve the
older debts.

e. The dependency on third parties (risk score 12)

Tab 14 Payzone Risk Report

@

Throughout this pandemic there is a risk to business-critical activities that have
a high dependency on third parties which have a possibility for high exposure,
for example, PLS which provide Payzone’s engineering resource. The key
suppliers were contacted and requested to complete a questionnaire to
understand their business continuity plan arrangements in place to enable
service levels to resume during the pandemic situation. Regular calls are in place
with key suppliers to monitor the service during this changeable situation.
Additional governance surrounding the control of suppliers is currently being
implemented with the development of a procurement policy. The
implementation of this policy will ensure the controls in place for external
providers are robust and minimises the risk in this area
f. Brexit (Black Swan risk score 5)

The risk to the operation is low based on an appraisal of suppliers and technology
processes and the only risk relates to the broader macro-economic impact to
the UK economy. This is being continually monitored during the weekly group
Covid-19/Brexit rapid response team calls.

Risk Appetite

4. The approach Payzone is adopting to develop the risk appetite is to have the Quality and
Risk Manager be a part of the Post Office team reviewing and updating the Post Office
Risk Appetite. This will ensure that Payzone aligns where possible to the Post Office Risk
Appetite statement. Once the Post Office Risk Appetite has been approved by ARC the risk
appetite statements will be reviewed and agreed by Payzone Board during the April
meeting.

Conclusion

5. Significant work has been conducted which has achieved a reduction in the overall risk
scoring of the pre-pandemic risks. Whilst the COVID 19 pandemic has changed the key
risks in the business, the overall risk profile has not changed significantly. Continuous
monitoring of how COVID 19 has impacted Bill Payments is in place to ascertain changes
to customer behaviour, volume impact, competitor behaviour, and the impact on the
operating model.

6. Whilst there has been good progress in the risk framework and maturing the risk culture
within Payzone there is still work to be completed to introduce the risk appetite statement.
This will be conducted in line with the POL group risk appetite statement. The technology
and legal and compliance risk appetite statements are due for approval at the November
ARC.

Next Steps & Timelines
7. Risk appetite be generated and brought to the Payzone Board in Q4 '21.

POST OFFICE LIMITED
RISK & COMPLIANCE COMMITTEE REPORT
Title: Law & Trends Report Hiei 12 November 2020 I
Author: Sarah Gray, Legal Director Sponsor: Ben Foat, Group General Counsel

Input Sought: Noting

The Committee is asked to note the new or proposed material changes to laws and regulations
since the last Risk & Compliance Committee (RCC), for onward submission to the Audit, Risk &
Compliance Committee (ARC).

Executive Summary

There are 4 matters for the Committee to note (details of which are set out in the Appendix):

1. Restriction of Public Sector Exit Payments Regulations 2020
The legislation implementing the £95k cap on exit payments comes into force on 4
November 2020. The cap will apply to any non-exempt termination payments that
represent a cost the employer including, redundancy payments, employer pension
contributions, and payment in lieu of notice.

2. Revenue and Customs Brief No.12 - VAT Treatment on Compensation Payments
HMRC published its Revenue and Customers Brief 12 (2020) that introduced their new
position on VAT treatment of contractual compensation payments. The result of this
approach by HMRC will mean that most compensation, early termination and cancellation
payments will be considered as payments for supply and will be liable for VAT.

3 HM Treasury Consultation on new Economic Crime Levy - Update
The Economic Crime levy aims to raise approximately £100 million per year from entities
regulated for Anti- Money Laundering (‘AML’) purposes and support reforms to the
sustainable resourcing of economic crime.

4. VAT treatment of Bill Payment products
Following a legal challenge from Paypoint, HMRC have changed their view on VAT

treatment of Bill Payment products. This change will increase the VAT recovery rate for
Post Office and Payzone.

HMRC have ruled that the income
earned from processing _ bill
payments for clients is now subject
to VAT and no longer VAT exempt as
it had been treated previously.

This rule change has come about
following a legal challenge made to
HMRC by Paypoint.

Post Office and Payzone (‘POL Group’)
are treated as one VAT Group for HMRC
purposes and therefore a joint approach
to this change is necessary.

HMRC are allowing the POL Group to
select a date to enact this change, the
sooner the change is enacted the
sooner the benefits can be claimed.

The POL Group will benefit financially
from this change as it will increase the
VAT recovery rate. It is anticipated that
this change will deliver an additional
c.£lm per year of additional VAT
recovery.

On top of this recovery, we may also be
eligible to submit a historic claim (going
back four years) for under-recovered
VAT. This would produce a one-off
windfall cash refund of c.£4m.

The POL Group cannot submit a historic
claim until the VAT change has been
corrected initially. The circumstances
around a historic claim are still in
discussion at this point, however we
understand than other companies have
done so which provides comfort to the
POL Group that we would also be able to.

finance has been set up and there is
funding for an initial month and a half of
work.

Previous Governance Oversight

The inappropriately archived branch files issue has previously been raised at the Risk &
Compliance Committee (RCC) and ARC meetings in September 2020.

Executive Summary

The paper addresses the situation in respect of the discovery of inappropriately archived branch
file documents whilst gathering information for responses to data requests from applicants to
the Historical Shortfall Scheme (“HSS”). It provides an update on the root cause analysis
(“RCA”), remediation activity and legal assessment of the Historical Matters-related and
Starling implications arising from the issue.

Increasingly management of data, in all formats, is a critical matter for all businesses. This

Paper notes the current, decentralised approach to data management in Post Office and
recommends that clearer accountabilities be allocated across the business

Conclusion

1. Concerns regarding data management in Post Office have arisen as a result of the

discovery of a number of archived branch files which had neither been structured nor
indexed appropriately. A comprehensive remediation plan has been put in place and,
subject to approval from the Committee, will be rolled out in Q3 on an expedited basis,
in coordination with the Post-Conviction Disclosure Exercise and Historical Shortfall
Scheme Activity.

2: To ensure that Post Office complies with its ongoing duty of disclosure as part of the GLO
“post-conviction disclosure exercise (“PCDE”), the recommendation is for external
lawyers to review the indices of archived boxes stored on Post Office’s behalf by Oasis,
by conducting key word searches, and dip testing both indexed and unindexed boxes.
The dip sampling exercise will then determine the extent to which any further disclosure
needs to be made (e.g. if the contents of the dip sampled boxes do not contain
disclosable material, then no further review may need to be undertaken; if however they
do contain disclosable material then it may be appropriate to widen the sample under
review).

3 As the Historical Shortfall Scheme (“HSS”) is a voluntary scheme, Post Office does not
have any procedural legal obligations to review material. However, in exercising its duty
of good faith to Postmasters, Post Office is taking reasonable and proportionate steps to
identify sources of material which are relevant to an application and will be following the
same search and dip testing processes as for the PCDE.

4. Post Office's disclosure obligation in Starling is

By To ensure that the GLO and Starling teams are sighted on relevant Post Office data (and
therefore to mitigate against a similar issue occurring again) the following activities are
planned / in progress:

a. All branches will be contacted via letter and asked to check and disclose all records
being held locally that should be archived, with updated procedural documents
provided outlining the process for archiving.

b. Data Property Services and Network are working together to identify the data
owners of the boxes already at Oasis which do not have indices and to get the
indices completed when an assessment against GDPR compliance will be made.

@ The Compliance Director will circulate to Data Owners, as the accountable people
for record retention, copies of the retention schedules and remediation logs and

records held by Post office have been made available to them.

6. Post Office must conduct reasonable and appropriate searches for information requested
as part of the DSAR process within GDPR. For the purpose of HMU requests, the HSS
data team have cross-referenced system data and conducted extensive searches in ten
different sources. This is time consuming but ensures Post Office is not in breach of
statutory obligations in respect of handling DSARS as these searches would be deemed
to be reasonable and appropriate.

a: Currently the Legal Hold Order that is in place in relation to the GLO and HMU work is a
recognised exemption to the requirement to hold information for no longer than is
necessary. The remediation logs from the Record Retention programme obliges the
business to have processes in place to delete all expired information once the hold order
is removed.

8. In respect to Post Office handling of FOI requests, the legislation obliges Post Office to
conduct reasonable and appropriate searches to locate in-scope information. FOI allows
Post Office to apply a time and cost exemption to locate the data, should these be
exceeded then the request can be rejected, including where searches are prolonged due
to poor record keeping practices. Therefore, as long as Post Office can evidence that the
necessary searches have been conducted then the risk of ICO intervention is low.

9. Data Governance in Post Office is managed through a number of different controls and
accountabilities. This is a decentralised approach and there is no single record depository
that enables the business to quickly identify and manage the data it holds. It is
recommended therefore that Post Office seeks to establish a single accountable unit for
data governance, supported by oversight from the CISO for data security and Compliance
for personal data protection.

Report

What was the RCA for the inappropriately archived branch files issue?

ie As previously reported in the September 2020 RCC, the data team, working on the HSS,
identified inappropriately archived boxes held at Oasis', our archive provider, which
might have relevance to the HSS DSARs. However, it was not possible to determine
quickly what was held in those boxes and whether the material in them was of any
relevance to the DSARs.

2. Initial investigations on a small sample suggest that branches have not being following
the archiving processes for branch records.
3. When a branch closes/closed an archiving process is meant to be followed. This involves

empty file boxes being sent to the branch and a list of requirements for archiving to be
completed. A list of contents is meant to be put in the archive box. Other than branch
name and FAD code, there does not appear to have been any external indication on the
contents of the box and Oasis do not open boxes at site.

4. The contents of the boxes may contain any branch balancing hard copies, Trading
statements, daily and weekly reports. They may also contain HR files such as P250
assistant verification and contractual information on the agent/postmaster.

What remediation actions have been / are being taken?

Ss Where the HSS data team have requested personal data for DSARS from incorrectly
indexed boxes, additional searches have been conducted with the business area to locate
the personal data. To date, the HSS team have been able to obtain the required data
through cross referencing across multiple systems data and combining information and
provide Post Masters with shortfall information.

6. Processes have been developed to ensure that we can meet our obligations or prove that
we have conducted the appropriate searches to meet the ‘reasonable and appropriate’
test.

Digital data / MI:

7. The Data Governance team in IT is conducting a review of the digital data/MI RACI.

8. There are 3 clear priorities to be progressed if Post Office is to manage its data asset
with the same degree of rigour as it does other enterprise assets. These priorities are:

a. ‘Fix the foundations’ - correct the weaknesses in core data management disciplines
and governance

b. Validate and deliver prioritised MI requirements to the business

G Confirm the approach and plan to progress the overall information strategy
(including development of a more detailed set of requirements, operating model,
and business case and to transition to a new MI organisation).

Branch document retention and archiving:

9. A plan is being implemented to ensure that any documents held in branches that should
be archived in accordance with the archive standards are disclosed, properly indexed
and submitted to Post Office's offsite storage (Oasis Records Management). Also, activity
is being undertaken to ensure that processes for record retention in Post Office, as

been included in a ‘release all data’ DSAR then Post Office would provide that
information to the requestor, if disclosable. It should be noted that outside of HMU
we have never had any reason to search branch file information to service a DSAR.

fen As part of the remediation plan, Data Protection will work with Property Services
and Network teams to;

i. identify the owners to allow the correct record retention schedules and
indexes to be applied. As there is no evidence that any individual has
suffered and harm, damage or distress then this is not a notifiable incident
to the ICO. Key to this is demonstrating that remediation plans are
progressed.

ii. consider whether any recent DSARs have been processed that would have
included requests for information from this source (Please note a search of
all non-HMU DSARs received in the last three years would not have required
any search of these boxes. For HMU DSARs we have been able to locate
information requested by alternative means).

What is the legal assessment of the implications for “Historical Matters”?

12. With respect to past prosecutions brought as a private prosecutor, Post Office owes a
post-conviction duty to disclose material to defendants that might cast doubt on the
safety of their conviction, and to make enquiries where there is a real prospect that the
enquiry would reveal such material. The method by which these duties are discharged
is through a “post-conviction disclosure exercise” (“PCDE”).

13. With respect to the Historical Shortfall Scheme (“HSS”), Post Office does not have any
procedural legal obligations concerning disclosure as it is a voluntary scheme. However,
following the GLO Common Issues Judgment, Post Office owes a duty of good faith to
postmasters requiring it to deal with postmasters fairly and transparently, a principle
reflected in the HSS's Terms of Reference and Q&A’s. Post Office is addressing this by
taking reasonable and proportionate steps to identify sources of material which are
relevant to an application (the standard adopted in conventional civil court proceedings).

14. In addition to this, Post Office has an obligation to conduct reasonable and appropriate
searches for Personal Data requested through the DSAR process. It is a reasonable
assumption that if the archived boxes were indexed correctly then these would be
considered ‘relevant filing systems’ for the purpose of GDPR and in scope for future
searches. However, given that the information required for the HSS DSARS has been
collated through other cross business searches then there is no breach of the GDPR.

15. Post Office initially addressed the impact by reviewing available indices to identify boxes
which might contain material relevant to the PCDE or HSS, and extract from those boxes
any material required to be disclosed as part of the PCDE, or which would be relevant to
the consideration of an HSS application.

Confidential

Post Office Limited - Risk and Compliance Committee-12/11/20 177 of 226

POL-BSFF-0238386_0176
POL00423571
POL00423571

16. Subsequent to receiving approval from the Historical Matters Steering Committee, for
both the PCDE and HSS, Post Office is addressing the issues identified through:

a.

Key word searches being applied (or in the case of previous searches, re-run)
across the expanded set of indices to identify boxes which may contain relevant
material, which will then be reviewed to identify relevant material;

Undertaking a “dip sample” exercise of a statistically representative random group
of indexed and unindexed boxes (c.100 of each) to assess the extent to which
they contain material relevant to the PCDE (which would be disclosed as part of
the PCDE) or the HSS work (which would be considered as part of the investigation
into a specific application).

The results of the dip sample will inform the next steps that may need to be taken
with respect to the remaining boxes (e.g. further reviews may be required if the
sample identifies significant volumes of material relevant to the PCDE and/or
HSS).

17. These steps (which are being carried out on an expedited basis in coordination with the
PCDE and HSS), combined with the remediation actions described above, will give
confidence that Post Office has addressed the obligations described above to review
known sources of materials for the PCDE and HSS.

What is the status of data governance in Post Office today?

23. Data governance in Post Office is managed through a number of different controls and
accountabilities. This is a decentralised approach and there is no single record depository
that enables the business to quickly identify and manage the data it holds.

Existing key controls

24. POL needs to manage its data to operate appropriately and effectively. In order to do
this a number of controls both at the enterprise, group and function level have been
established outlining levels of accountability and responsibility.

25. These controls are set out, principally, through the following policies:
a. Cyber & Information Security Policy (principally a technical IT policy)
i. Acceptable use standards
ii. Access controls standard
iii. Asset management standard

iv. Encryption standard
v. Information classification standard
vi. Network [IT network] security standard guidelines
vii. Platform security guidelines
viii. Platform security standards
ix. Secure development lifecycle guidelines
b. Document Retention and Disposal Policy

i. The Record Retention programme, completed in Q4 2019/20, identified the
Data Owners and data held, which was put into the record retention
schedules

ii. A GE re-prioritisation exercise in February 2019 resulted in the Record
Retention Programme'’s funding being halved (from £1.6m down to £0.8m)
and remediation being de-scoped, save for providing IT solutions to high-
risk areas to automate the adherence to these schedules for Telecoms
(Fujitsu), POI (Home insurance, pricing & analytics, Travel insurance, MI
and HR), the Brands database and HR (Success factors & SAP).

& Protecting Personal Data Policy

26. The Document Retention & Disposal and Protecting Personal Data policies set out the
control standards that Data Owners must ensure are adhered to. The key controls are:

a. As part of the design of a new product or service, or where a product or service is
being updated, product or service risks must be considered, mitigated and
documented before completion of design phase. This must include updating of any
related Document Retention Schedules;

b. The integrity and accuracy of data must be ensured at the point of collection.

G Data Owners are also responsible for maintenance and adherence of their
retention schedules. All Data Owners must ensure that the retention schedules for
their area are up to date. This is especially important when changes are being
implemented to business processes.

8
Confidential

Post Office Limited - Risk and Compliance Committee-12/11/20 179 of 226

POL-BSFF-0238386_0178
POL00423571
POL00423571

Tab 16 Data

@

d. Data Owners must understand the complete information lifecycle (creation,
capture, index, manage, access, retrieve, administer, repurpose, share, retain,
dispose, preserve) for all data within their sphere of control.

e. Data Owners must ensure that they have defined the storage requirements for
the data under their sphere of control, and that this has been documented and
agreed. This particularly applies where encryption is required. This is a field within
the retention schedule.

27. Each team within each business unit has a record retention schedule in place. This
schedule details the records they create / hold, where they are stored, their classification,
retention period, storage instructions and end of period action.

28. These schedules are stored centrally on the CISO SharePoint Site and were produced by
the Record Retention Programme.

29. Once produced, each schedule was signed off and approved by the relevant GE-1
member (and supporting team) with responsibility for remediation, adherence and
keeping them up to date handed over to the relevant GE-1 member(s), in accordance
with the Group Retention and Disposal Policy. This responsibility was communicated to
each ‘Data Owner’.

Next Steps:

30. Completion of the remediation activity on an expedited basis in coordination with the
Post-Conviction Disclosure Exercise and Historical Shortfall Scheme Activity

31. Lawyers to conclude the actions in respect of the assessment of all boxes stored at Oasis,
on behalf of Post Office.

32. GE to agree which business function has overall accountability for data governance,
supported by oversight from the CISO for data security and Compliance for personal data
protection.

POST OFFICE LIMITED
RISK & COMPLIANCE COMMITTEE REPORT

Title: Procurement Governance & Meeting Date: I 12 November 2020
Compliance Report

muthar Barbara Brannon, Procurement Sponsor: Alisdair Cameron, Group Chief
Director Finance Officer

Input Sought: Noting

The Committee is asked to review the report and note that no Procurement Risk Exceptions
submitted to the Post Office Limited Board since September 2002 and to consider and give
direction in respect of the contracts in the Procurement pipeline which are high value and at
risk of being awarded or extended non-compliantly.

The Committee is also asked to note the alteration in governance approved by ARC and to
advise on preferred governance processes in respect of subthreshold risk exception requests.

Previous Governance Oversight

e July 2020 - Quarterly Risk Report
e September 2020 - Board Report

Executive Summary

As a business in receipt of public funds Post Office Limited (POL) is bound by the Public Contract
Regulations (2015). PCR 2015 oblige POL to behave in a fair, objective & transparent way when
contracting with 3 party suppliers. Additionally, set procedures must be followed for spend
above £25k and £189k.

The purpose of this report is to set out both breaches to Post Office governance and key controls
around contracts and compliance to PCR regulation in the award of contracts.

The aim of collating this information is to drive improvement in awareness and compliance
behaviour across the organisation. The second and primary aim is to work with GE and Business
Units to commence commercial reviews in a more timely way ensuring POL obtains value,
commercial and contractual flexibility fitting the requirements and business strategy of the
organisation.

In March 2020, Post Office Board requested prior approval of all Exceptions. This was revised
in September 2020 to above threshold Exceptions >£189k only in a revision to existing
governance. From November 2020 sub threshold exceptions will be reported retrospectively to
RCC and to ARC.

A Procurement Risk Exception Note is required to accompany all Exception Requests and a
Legal Risk note for requests >£189k.

2. What are we doing about it?
Active reviews continue with Business Units with the highest values relating to non-

Report

5. What are the potential consequences of non-compliant awards?

a) Pre-contractual remedies overview: During a Procurement, an aggrieved party can
seek an interim injunction suspending the tender or the implementation until the court
decides on an outcome.

b) Post-contractual remedies: The court can order an ‘ineffectiveness order’ rendering
the contract void &/or can award damages.

6. Why are these incidents of non-compliance occurring, and what can be done about it?

@

Non-compliant awards may be made for a number of reasons at the Post Office.

ig Approval 17

a) Low value, time constrained or highly sensitive/specialist engagements are not
uncommon.

b) Large commercial arrangements cannot often be easily competed or unravelled
without operational impact, and re-procurement may be subject to a pending evolution
of a supporting Business Strategy and/or completion of large, and complex technical
programmes of work to maintain or enhance services prior to a possible exit.

c) The contractual arrangements may pre-date PCR 2015 regulations or the contract
novated during separation from RMG, automatically becoming non-compliant at the
renewal point. Non-compliant awards are frequently made on a tactical basis to extend
contractual services while public tender processes are executed.

d) Delays to public sector panels of suppliers becoming available. The Post Office makes
extensive use of this low-cost route to market and new/refreshed panels are subject
to frequent delays from Crown Commercial Services. Single interim extensions [of
periods under 12 months] while tender processes are run are considered to be low
risk legally.

e) Changes in scope or value over the term of a contract may render the extension or
renewal of services non-compliant. Material changes to the scope of a contract may
render the whole contract non-compliant.

f) Disregard for, or lack of understanding of the regulations.

7. Why are we receiving this report?
A decision to collate this information into a single location was taken in the Autumn of
2016. The aim is to track and improve our overall compliance and commercial results as
an organisation, while also ensuring perceptions are accurate. However, it should be noted
that it will facilitate timely responses to Freedom of Information requests which adds risk
to the Post Office commercial landscape.

8. Are any of these breaches arguable on regulatory grounds or are they all breaches?

A full explanation of the individual compliance breaches for direct awards over £189k
[previously £164k & £181k] threshold is attached in Appendix 1. Each entry details the
nature of, and the value of the breach. The threshold is altered every two years based on
the FX rate between GBP and the Euro.

The Procurement Compliance Register does not at present give an indicative risk level
attached to the award. This information is provided to the accountable executives under
internal governance processes in the form of a PCR risk note before a contract above
threshold is entered into, and if necessary, under Legal Privilege. In addition, all
signatories to a contract have sight of the Risk note as part of the Contract Authorisation
Form [CAF].

All entries are compliance breaches. A period of challenge applies to each PCR breach once
an aggrieved party becomes aware or ought to have become aware. This risk finally
expires at 6 years from the date of breach. The defensibility of a legal challenge is outlined
within a Risk Note.

Describe what you are doing about the breaches. Where we are in breach, do we have a

plan to come back into compliance and over what time period will that plan take effect?

a) A forward view of material contracts falling under each Business Unit is currently
prepared by the relevant Procurement Manager for discussions with their key
stakeholders. The maturity of this look ahead view does vary currently and is
consistently a high priority activity within the team.

b) Sourcing options papers are prepared for review by contract managers and key
stakeholders [risk, legal, security] with routes to market agreed. In many cases these
are dependent on evolving business and operating model strategies and the
Procurement team are actively involved helping to advise and review options as
thinking evolves.

c) Where a non-compliant award is proposed due to time pressure, Procurement are
actively working on long term mitigation with awards made on an interim basis to
meet urgent operational needs.

d) Each RCC member now receives a regular report on compliance within their business
unit[s].

e) A Risk & Governance process requires a Risk Exception report to be created for non-
compliant direct awards with GE sign off.

f) Awards over £189k must have prior Board approval before being entered into.

g) All Professional Services engagements must be approved in writing in advance by the
CFO/COO. A compliant panel of preferred consulting partners has been appointed and
proposed engagements outside of this panel are subject to additional review and
challenge.

h) Procurement provides training as part of the revised Induction process for new staff.
Training packs are being updated for existing staff and a new training module made
available on Successfactors. Ad hoc training sessions for interested Business Units are
also run.

i) Anew Intranet site has been launched for Procurement to improve visibility of process,
regulation, and the panels of approved compliant suppliers available to POL business
units.

j) Arevised POL Procurement Policy and supporting processes is in progress giving more
granular guidance.

k) Using Crown Commercial Services frameworks, panels of Preferred Suppliers are being
refreshed and updated across a wide range of spend categories to reduce time to
market, improve compliance and greatly improve commercial outcomes and legal risk.

1) A planned change to operational systems will, once live, give Procurement earlier
visibility of potential compliance issues eg: contractual value thresholds.

Risk Assessment, Mitigations & Legal Implications

ig Approval 17

13. As a business in receipt of public funds POL is bound by the Public Contract Regulations
(2015). PCR 2015 oblige POL to behave in a fair, objective & transparent way when
contracting with 3" party suppliers. Additionally, set procedures must be followed for
spend above £25k and £189k.

14. Failure to abide by the legislation or “slicing and dicing” contracts exposes POL to risk,
both as far the commercial outcomes of the contracts as well as the reputational damage,
legal remedies, censure & fines that can follow the discovery of a breach. Our compliance
to PCR can be requested under a Freedom of Information request at any time.

15. The PCR Compliance Register allows for the tracking of breaches to PCR regulations at the
Post Office and internal governance processes. One aim of collating this information is to
drive improvement in awareness and compliance behaviour across the organisation. The
second and primary aim is to work with GE and Business Units to commence commercial
reviews in a more timely way ensuring POL obtains value, commercial and contractual
flexibility fitting the requirements and business strategy of the organisation.

16. Contract and financial governance policy and processes at Post Office are set by the Legal,
Risk and Governance team with clear guidelines for staff availably on the Company
Secretariat team intranet site. This sets out steps to be taken to obtain financial and

contractual approvals prior to making a binding commitment to an external party. Non-
compliance to internal governance processes are also captured within this report.

Risk Title End User Compute - Termination Assistance/Exit Services Risk

Detail of contract at risk of exception I This note is to explain the residual risk in relation to using a contractual mechanism
request and i called the Termination Assistance Period within the Post Office Limited (POL) End User
Computing (EUC) with Computacenter (CC).

The contract covers provision and support for all of POL’s Colleague, (e.g. Laptops,
printers, central login mechanism, etc.), Branch end user compute environments (e.g.
Counter hardware that executes Horizon, receipt printers, PEDs, etc.) as well as Shared
Services (e.g. components used by both Colleague and Branch such as Microsoft Active
Directory).

This contract has been in place since 30 April 2015 and POL has already utilised all
available compliant options for extension. Our contract will end on the 29 April 2021,
and this end date is known by other providers of similar services (DXC, Accenture and,
sec).

Based on the remaining time on the CC contract, the time to prepare for and then run
a competition(s), followed by the time to transition services, it is not possible for POL
to exit and transition all services before the 29 April 2021 contact end date, regardless
of which strategy is utilised.

POL will therefore need to utilise a contract mechanism called the Termination
Assistance Period (TAP).

The TAPs primary use is to allow Computacenter to continue to deliver live services
whilst a new incumbent (or POL) transitions services away.

POL must give CC at least 4 months notice, by 29 December 2020, to commence
services under the TAP which can then run for a maximum of 24 months, with an option
to extend the Termination Services for a further 6 months.

The TAP must be used for exit activities only and cannot be used to simply extend or
transform the existing service.

The TAP was put in place during the preferred bidder stage of the procurement for the
current contract and had not been part of negotiations with the wider market.

Legal advice was provided in relation to that risk at the point of approval of the EUC
‘Agreement. This advice identified the risk as low as transition services over the TAP
timescales are not unusual for an ICT contract of this type and because it was envisaged
that, at the time of the use of the TAP, procurement(s) would be underway for
replacement services and so interested bidders would be motivated not to challenge.

This means that by April 2021, POL must be demonstrably and overtly in the process of
exiting the existing contract.

The procurement plan for replacing the current CC End User Compute contract is to
split the existing contract into 3 parts, each procured separately.

Why is the chosen option now at risk
