At its meeting on O1 July 2020 GE endorsed a recommendation to compete the
procurement exercise for new contract(s), (3yr + 2yr), before April 2021 with transition
completed by Sept 2021.

This strategy provided the greatest opportunity for optimising savings (due to deal size)
and via a structured procurement. This requires an investment of £6.11M and is the
existing strategic direction (as of December 2019), albeit with greater utilisation of the
TAP than originally envisaged due to Covid19 delays. This would allow us to proceed to
market in a standard, structured fashion with a view of transitioning services to a new
supplier.

This potentially offers only lower (but predictable) in year OPEX savings which are
currently estimated at approximately <£750K. There is however a greater possibility of
obtaining on-going OPEX savings post 2022/23 (assuming 21/22 is lost due to transition
charges) as a result of the tendering activity. This could be in the region of £1.5M pa post
transition and transformation.

POST OFFICE PAGE 1 OF 4
CONFIDENTIAL AND LEGALLY PRIVILEGED

Risk Note

Author: Suzie Miles (Commercial) and Lucy Woods (Procurement) - Ashfords LLP Date: 03 November 2020

Summary

Post Office Limited (“POL”) must give Computacenter a Termination Assistance Notice by
29 December 2020 at the latest to trigger a Termination Assistance Period. The TAP shall
end no later than 29 April 2023. During the TAP CC shall, at the request of POL: (i) continue
to provide the Services with phased transition to a Replacement Contractor; and/or (ii)
provide Termination Services. While technically there is no clause entitling POL to extend
the TAP, the EUC Agreement does provide that POL can extend the provision of the
Termination Services and services that are the same or similar to the Services for up to 6
months beyond the TAP using the Change Control Procedure, which is akin to extending
the TAP beyond 24 months. Furthermore, POL can also reduce the period of the TAP using
the Change Control Procedure.

POL is only required to issue a Termination Assistance Notice to request Termination
Services during a TAP. Notwithstanding this there are provisions stating that POL can
request the Supplier to provide the Services during the TAP as well as the Termination
Services or on its own without any Termination Services. It is therefore unclear how POL
would trigger the TAP if it only wanted the Services to be continued and not any
Termination Services. Our advice would be that POL still issue a Termination Assistance
notice and detail any high level Termination Services that it may require at any stage
during the TAP, including access to information.

Background

POL and Computacenter (UK) Limited (“CC”) entered into the End User Computing
Services Agreement on 29" April 2014 (“EUC Agreement”). On 29 November 2019 POL
and CC signed a letter of extension to extend the EUC Agreement for a further 12-month
period commencing on 30 April 2020, which means the EUC Agreement will expire on 29
April 2021 (“2019 Letter of Extension”). POL does not have another option to extend
the EUC Agreement after this extension.

POL is considering re-procuring the services under the EUC Agreement. POL does not wish
to terminate the EUC Agreement early but wants to explore the possibility of triggering a
Termination Assistance Period (“TAP”).

This note provides a summary of the (i) procurement risks and (ii) commercial risks related
to triggering the TAP under the EUC Agreement.

Unless specified otherwise, defined terms under this risk note have the same meaning as
under the EUC Agreement.

Commercial risk note

Term and expiry

Under clause 66.1, the EUC Agreement commences on the date of signature (the Effective
Date, being 29" April 2014) (note that we have not seen a dated version of the EUC
Agreement but this is as detailed in the letter of extension) and expires at the end of the

Term (being the Initial Term and the Extension Period). POL does not need to take any
action to effect the expiry of the EUC Agreement.

1

196 of 226 Post Office Limited - Risk and Compliance Committee-12/11/20

POL-BSFF-0238386_0195
POL00423571
POL00423571

The Initial Term is 4 years from the Service Commencement Date (being 30 April 2015,
as per Schedule 1) and POL has 2 options to extend the Initial Term for Extension Periods
of up to 12 months each (clause 66.3).

The 2019 Letter of Extension specifies that the Term is extended to 29 April 2021.
Charges

During the TAP, POL shall continue to pay for the Services. The 2019 Letter of Extension
calculated the reduction to the Charges for the Services in FY19/20 and FY20/21. POL shall
additionally pay for any Termination Services, Knowledge Transfer or reasonable
assistance based on the Rate Card and as agreed in advance with POL. The Charges for
the Services and Termination Services shall be re-calculated for the TAP.

All outgoings and expenses, rents, royalties and other periodic payments in respect of
Assets and Sub-contracts transferred to POL or the Replacement Contractor shall be
apportioned between POL, CC and the Replacement Contractor, as applicable (paragraph
5.4, Schedule 8.5).

Termination Assistance Period

Duration

The TAP shall end no later than 29 April 2023 (not longer than 24 months after the expiry
of the Term (Schedule 1, Schedule 8.5 and 2019 Letter of Extension)), but POL has the
right to extend the Termination Services for another 6 months beyond the TAP.

The Services

During the TAP, CC is required to continue to provide the Services to the required Service
Levels and no degradation in the standards of the Services (clause 69.1; paragraph 6.1
Schedule 8.5).

Termination Services

CC shall additionally, if requested by POL, provide the Termination Services. To request
the Termination Services, POL must give CC a Termination Assistance Notice by no later
than 29 December 2020 (4 months prior to expiry (paragraph 2.3(c)(ii)(D), 2019 Letter
of Extension)). Note that under Schedule 8.5, paragraph 6.9, the notice period for a
Termination Assistance Notice is 3 months but this has been amended by the 2019 Letter
of Extension. POL is not required to give notice for CC to continue to provide the Services
during the TAP.

The Termination Assistance Notice shall specify: (i) the date from which Termination
Services are required, which may be up to 12 months prior to expiry of the Agreement;
(ii) the nature of the Termination Services required; and (iii) the period which it is
anticipated that Termination Services will be required, which shall continue no longer than
24 months after the expiry date. However please note that POL has an option to extend
the Termination Services for up to 6 months beyond that 24-month TAP period by giving
CC no later than 20 Working Days prior to the date on which the provision of Termination
Services is due to expire (Schedule 8.5, para 6.10). Paragraph 6.14 of Schedule 8.5 details
the scope of Termination Services which are mainly to assist and support the transition.

POL-BSFF-0238386_0196
POL00423571
POL00423571

Tab 17 Procurement Governance & Compliance Report & Barclays Cheque Clearing Approval 17

POL may terminate the requirement for Termination Services by serving no less than 20
Working Days written notice upon CC. This shall not have the effect of reducing the
maximum possible duration of the TAP being 24 months after expiry of the Term.

Changes to the Services and Termination Services:

Under the 2019 Letter of Extension, the Services and Termination Services provided
according to Termination Assistance Notice may be amended using the Change Control
Procedure during the TAP, including to extend or reduce any time periods for the provision
of any such Service or Termination Service. POL’s right to terminate the TAP early for
convenience after expiry of the Agreement would not apply as the clause does not survive
expiry of the EUC Agreement.

Exit Plan

CC is required to provide an initial Exit Plan within 3 months from the Effective Date then
provide the final Exit Plan no less than 6 months prior to the expiry of the EUC Agreement.

CC must review the Exit Plan annually and prepare a revised Exit Plan to reflect the
changes in the Services and submit it to POL. The parties must then agree the content
together. There is no provision for POL to initiate a request for changes to an Exit Plan but
practically speaking, POL may raise such request during the review process of an Exit Plan.

If the parties cannot agree the final Exit Plan within 14 days from CC’s delivery of the final
Exit Plan to POL then the matter will be escalated in accordance with Schedule 8.1
(Governance) to be resolved by both parties within 5 Working Days from the escalation
before going through the Dispute Resolution Procedure (paragraph 6.8, Schedule 8.5).
Until such dispute is resolved, the last approved version of the Exit Plan will apply.

Transition

The transition of the Services may be phased (paragraph 6.6, Schedule 8.5). If the
transition is not completed during the TAP, POL may request in writing that CC continue
to provide Termination Services and additional services, including that are same or similar
to the Services, on a time and material basis using the Rate Card (subject to indexation)
following the TAP and until the transition has been effected (paragraph 2.3(c)(iv), 2019
Letter of Extension). The notice period for such request is not specified.

Procurement risk note

Residual Procurement Risk

There is a residual procurement risk attached to the use of the TAP from the point
at which it was introduced into the EUC Agreement at the Preferred Bidder stage
of the procurement for the EUC Agreement because it did not form part of the
dialogue with bidders. Legal advice was provided in relation to that risk at the point
of approval of the EUC Agreement. This advice identified the risk as low as
transition services over the TAP timescales are not unusual for a ICT contract of
this type and because it was envisaged that, at the time of the use of the TAP,
procurement(s) would be underway for replacement services and so interested
bidders would be motivated not to challenge.

At this stage, this residual procurement risk still applies and the use of the TAP
has the potential to highlight this procurement risk as we believe that the market

3

198 of 226 Post Office Limited - Risk and Compliance Committee-12/11/20

POL-BSFF-0238386_0197
POL00423571

POL00423571

erriance &

is aware that the contract is due to terminate at the end of April 2021 and therefore
will become aware that additional transition services have been agreed.

The use of the Services during the TAP

The Services and the Termination Services are identified separately in Schedule
8.5 of the EUC Agreement. Paragraph 6.1 makes it clear that CC has to provide the
Services during the TAP and that POL can choose what Termination Services it
requires.

Given that the procurements for the replacement services will be underway by the
time the TAP begins, POL may consider the provision of the Services during this
time is enabling the transition. There could be an argument made that this is not
the case unless the Termination Services are also being provided quite quickly into
the TAP, but this is not necessarily supported by the wording of Schedule 8.5. For
this reason the more quickly the re-procurements are carried out the lower this
risk.

Mitigating factors

Despite the risks attached to the use of the TAP outlined above, we consider that
there are several factors mitigating these risks of successful challenge so that they
remain low.

Firstly, we understand that the bidders from the original procurement who are most
likely to become aware that the TAP has been agreed post Preferred Bidder stage
given their knowledge of contract during the process are potential bidders for the
re-procurements and so they are less likely to be motivated to challenge at this
stage.

Secondly, any challenge would be limited to a damages claim because both a
declaration of ineffectiveness and a penalty will be time barred. Bringing a damages
claim when the timescale of the alleged ‘breach’ is limited to a few months while a
procurement process is completed is likely to be advised against by legal advisors
to a potential challenger.

The value of the Services during the TAP is estimated to be £5 million, which added
to the £66 million spend under the EUC to date, is well within the value of up to
£300 million set out in the OJEU notice. The OJEU notice also sets out that
transition services will be provided after the termination date.

Even if the TAP could not be used to provide the Services post termination, it is
likely that the provision of the Services would fall under the ability to modify a
contract under Regulation 72(1)(b) in any event. While we understand that CC
would be unlikely to agree to such an extension on the same terms and therefore
this way forward is not an option, it does assist with an assessment that the risk
of successful challenge in a Court is low.

Detail of contract being entered into /

Exception I Regulation Breach Exception ID To be provided by
Category Procurement

Blue Yonder (formerly JDA Software Group) is an American software and consultancy
company that has ended up owning and delivering support to POL of a bespoke
version of the WMD (Warehouse Management Dispatcher).

Blue Yonder having initially agreed to work through a compliant IT Reseller
Framework in June of this year to bring the contract under compliance have reneged
and refused to operate in such a way this week (WC 2/11). The company have only
elaborated that they are not set up to work through resellers in this way and are not
willing to invest time or effort in an approach to payments that they will not use
elsewhere. We still have a need for the services, the renewal is shortly due, hence
this PREN-there are no other avenues to achieve compliance.

Context:
“Swindon Stocks” comprises a series of legacy IT systems focused around Galaxy

The Galaxy system acts as the main hub for the stock control system and holds master
data for all products and address details for Branch, Royal Mail, Parcel Force and third
parties.

In relation to products, Galaxy stores approximately 11,000 products 30% of which are
active at any given time.

* Holds a large variety of master data about items, delivery sites and supplier contracts
* Keeps track of stock availability

* Takes in orders from POL branches and other warehouse client sites

* Reserves stock, if available

* Consolidates orders per delivery address and Passes orders to WCS for picking, packing
and dispatch

* Case management for customer queries

* Provides our back office financial systems with data so that clients can be billed.

Procurement Risk Exception Form

Galaxy receives orders from branches, as well as Royal Mail and Parcel Force depots,
and fulfils them by interfacing with WCS and Mercia; note that it has both POL and RMG
users.

Galaxy acts as a hub, with WCS (aka WMD), Mercia, POLSAP, Royal Mail and Parcel
Force systems as spokes. A number of Access databases are used in conjunction with

All of the other components have confirmed and compliant procurement routes for

Risk Note

Author: Ravi Mudundi Date: 04 Nov. 20

Risk Report

This is a Legal risk report prepared in respect of an agreement to provide software that
is used within the Swindon supply chain stock centre to control the pick and
pack/conveyor belt - “Warehouse Control System” (“Agreement”) between Post Office
Limited (“POL”) and (“Blue Yonder”).

Background and Purpose

I understand the Agreement was compliantly sourced in 2015:
Blue Yonder provides a software (JDA Warehouse Management Dispatcher), and
support/maintenance for stock management systems located in Swindon (“Services”)

The Agreement is due to expire on 15th November 2020 and POL has secured the
Services beyond the expiry of the Agreement, via a reseller under the Health Trust
Europe (HTE) Framework Agreement. POL appointed SCC as its reseller under the HTE
Framework Agreement. POL has carried out. this exercise in order to compliantly source
the Services.

Whilst Blue Yonder were originally keen to provide the Services via SCC, they are now
refusing to do so on the basis that-they are not set up to work through resellers. POL is
still engaging with Blue Yonder to enter into the arrangement. If Blue Yonder refuses to
enter into an agreement via'the reseller, then POL will have to renew the Agreement
non-compliantly with Blue-Yonder for continuation of the Services.

The purpose of this risk report is to summarise the key risks to POL if the Agreement is
non-compliantly extended and the mitigating factors assigned to such risk.

Tab 17 Procurement Governance & Compliance Report & Barclays Cheque Cles

1. What contracted services are being extended and why

ig Approval 17

Questions asked & addressed

2. What is the background to this request?

3. What options were considered?

4. What is required to re-procure these services?

Report

What contracted services will need to be extended and why?

5. Cheque transactions support core services such as Mails (stamps and parcels); Bill
Payments (e.g., utilities); and PO Money Savings/ISAs. In 2019/20, a total of c1.9m
cheques and c8.4m Partner Bank Envelopes were processed, at an OPEX cost of c£1.2m.
By not continuing the current service with Barclays, it would result in cheques not being
accepted across our branch counters as a method of payment and breach our contractual
commitment on cheque deposit service with Banks. This would impact our credibility with
customers, require contract changes with our partners who accept cheques for their
services (e.g. DVLA, Bill Payments etc) and our ability to negotiate Banking Framework
3. We are committed under Banking Framework 2 to keep the deposit service until
December 2022.

What other options have been considered?

6. An OJEU procurement process could be prepared and launched for a replacement AS IS
service, however the current service loses c£3m p.a. mainly due to the Royal Mail
overnight pouch service (c£4.4. p.a.) and a minimum term of 2-3 years would have to
be offered to the market in order to make it attractive to bid. Hence, there is a wish to
explore other commercial options via an RFI which was issued to the market in on
4/11/20. This will provide key market information that will mean we are better informed
on what cheque processing option to procure (e.g., costs, solution risks and delivery
timescales).

7. In parallel we are also exploring the opportunities to include the Camelot/Postal Order
Corporate Banking contract which could help save on procurement, business and contract
management resource if one supplier can provide both services.

Banking Framework 3 will provide the opportunity to either significantly increase the ‘as is’
cheque deposit service price to banks, possibly increased further with the offer of processing
from a central point into clearing on banks’ behalf (as we do with our MOP cheques), or offer
an in-branch scanning solution if the RFI and resulting business case justify such investment,
in particular that the cost base can be moved to a predominantly variable basis given the
likely fall off in cheque volumes.

POST OFFICE PAGE 1 OF 3
CONFIDENTIAL AND LEGALLY PRIVILEGED

Risk Note

Author: Lucy Woods (Procurement) - Ashfords LLP Date: 23 June 2020

Summary
Post Office Limited (“POL”) is seeking procurement advice in relation to a 12 month
extension to its cheque clearing services.

POL can seek to use the exemptions in Regulation 72 of the PCR 2015 and the risk of such
exemptions being effective if challenged in Court is medium, but that when assessed
against the actual likelihood of challenge we consider this risk is low.

POL can further mitigate these risks of challenge by ensuring it publishes the required
notices in the OJEU.

Background

Post Office Limited ("POL") and Barclays Banks Plc ("Barclays") entered into an
agreement dated 7 May 2010 for the provision of cheque processing and related services
(the “Bulk Clearing Contract"). We understand that the Bulk Clearing Contract
originally had a maximum overall contract term of 8 years; an estimated value of £10
million; and was procured in accordance with the Public Contracts Regulations 2006, now
replaced with the Public Contracts Regulations 2015 (the "PCR 2015"). The OJEU notice
referred to a term of 5 years with an option to extend ‘for three years or more’.

The Bulk Clearing Contract was amended:

*® on or around 28 September 2016, to extend the initial term to 31 October
2016;

e on 25 November 2016, to amend and restate the contract. The amendments
included an extension of the contract term to 31 July 2017; and

e in 2017 by a Deed of Variation to provide for an extension of the contact term
until 30 June 2018, along with an additional right for POL to extend to 30
June 2020. As part of this Deed of Variation, the parties also agreed some
commercial changes to the contract.

POL is now looking to agree with Barclays a further 12 month extension to the Bulk
Clearing Contract, which would extend the contract to 30 June 2021 (the “BCC Dov").
Such extension also provides for some further amendments to the contract terms,
including some amendments to liability for POL and Barclays and some review to the
charges over the extension term. POL would like advice on the procurement compliance
of the BCC Dov.

Behind the Deed of Variation there has been a complex background of the introduction of
the image clearing requirements in the industry (the “Image Clearing Obligation”). We
understand POL has continually reviewed the need to re-procure these services on the
open market, however the implementation of the Image Clearing Obligation has caused
significant delays to POL's ability to do that in a manner which does not affect services
and is value for money. Originally due to be completed in 2017, the Image Clearing
Obligation has seen the market struggle to meet the new obligations and as recently as
early 2020 the market has only just settled to a point where POL could look to start a
procurement with a sensible outcome.

212 of 226 Post Office Limited - Risk and Compliance Committee-12/11/20

POL-BSFF-0238386_0211
POL00423571
POL00423571

Tab 17 Procurement Governance & Compliance Report & Barclays Cheque Clee

ig Approval 17

Modification

The BCC DoV can be compliantly entered into provided that one of the exemptions set out
in Regulation 72 of the PCR 2015 applies because the changes to the Bulk Clearing
Contract represent a modification during its term. If one of the exemptions under
Regulation 72 cannot be used then the BCC DoV could be held to be an illegal direct award.

There are two exemptions we consider may apply to the BCC DoV, that under Regulation
72 (1) (b) and that under Regulation 72 (1) (c).

Regulation 72 (1) (b) allows for changes to the Bulk Clearing Contract to add additional
services provided that a change in contractor cannot be made because:

(a) of economic or technical reasons; and
(b) this would cause significant inconvenience or substantial duplication of costs.

We consider it is very likely that the Image Clearing Obligation had an effect which required
the Bulk Clearing Contract to be extended past its original 8 year term using this
exemption, however the Court would decide on the facts whether that was the case.

To be able to use this exemption, the total value of the services following the BCC DoV
must not exceed £15 million. It is our understanding that the estimate total spend across
the services to include the 12 month extension of the BCC DoV is £11.5 million.

Our concern about the use of this exemption is that it relates to the ‘addition of services’
and not changes to the contractual relationship generally. We understand that there have
been various amendments to the commercial positions between POL and Barclays during
the term (including SLAs historically) and the BCC DoV provides for both changes to the
indemnity and liabilities of POL and Barclays and the charges for the services. Accordingly
there is a risk that these changes are not purely the ‘addition of services’. To the extend
POL is comfortable that these changes are absolutely necessary due to the addition of the
services for the increased term (and not due to the changing commercial circumstances
of the parties) then we consider this exemption could be used. If POL is not confident in
this position it can consider the use of Regulation 72 (1) (c).

Regulation 72 (1) (c) can be used by POL for the BCC DoV where POL can demonstrate
that the changes have ‘been brought about by circumstances that a diligent contracting
authority could not have foreseen’. The benefit of this exemption is that it relates to all
changes and therefore can include commercial changes as well as the addition of services
provided that the changes do not change the overall nature of the contract. Again there
would be a financial limit of £15 million for the use of this exemption.

In our view POL may find it harder to use this exemption given that the Image Clearing
Obligation has been in place since 2017 and so lack of foresight is more difficult to
demonstrate at this stage, however, it may be that the difficulties that the market would
face with the Image Clearing Obligation over the last 3 years could not have been foreseen.
Again, this would be for the Court to decide on the facts but we anticipate POL could put
forward quite compelling evidence on this front having, as we understand it, looked to re-
procure several times but considering that the market was not ready to be able to bid
effectively.

The use of either exemption requires POL to publish a Modification Notice in the OJEU. We
note this was not done at the last extension which increases the risk of challenge and

2,

Post Office Limited - Risk and Compliance Committee-12/11/20 213 of 226

POL-BSFF-0238386_0212
POL00423571
POL00423571

Tab 17 Procurement Governance & Compliance Report & Barclays Cheque Clee

ig Approval 17

therefore we advise that this should be done this time to fully mitigate this risk (see section
on mitigation below). For the BCC DoV we consider the risk of not being able to use the
Regulation 72 exemptions as medium (but see below).

Consequences of an illegal direct award and likelihood of challenge
In the event it was held that the entry into the BCC DoV was an illegal direct award the
consequences of such a finding are:
a) a declaration of ineffectiveness which would bring the contracts to an end
with associated penalties; and/or
b) the award of damages by POL to the successful challenger.

To understand the likelihood of a challenge arising we need to consider the potential
challengers, which are those providers on the market who provide cheque clearing
services. A risk only crystallises if a challenge is brought.

Our understanding from POL is that the market has not been in a position to effectively
bid for these services if they had gone out to market at any point between 2017 and early
2020. To the extent this is correct then we can assume that the likelihood of a market
player wanting to bring a challenge is greatly reduced. POL needs to ensure that its
procurement strategy from early 2020 onwards allows for the services to be re-procured
in the most efficient way possible on the basis that the extensions are only being put in
place to cover the gap between the Image Clearing Obligations settling down to a point
where the market would be able to effectively bid and when a procurement could be
completed.

This assumption is supported by the fact that any market player who was interested in the
services would have been aware that the BCC Contract was due to end in 2018 according
to the OJEU notice and therefore POL may have expected a challenge before now, if there
was an appetite for a challenge on the market.

For this reason we would assess the actual likelihood of successful challenge as lower than
set out earlier in this note and would therefore consider it to be low.

Mitigations

By publishing notices in the OJEU in relation to the use of the exemptions set out above,
POL will be doing what it can to ‘notify’ the market and seek to set the time limit for
challenges running.

POL must balance this against the risk of highlighting the presence to the market of the
DoV however we would assume that the nature of the market is such that POL’s
relationship with Barclays is already well known.

For a claim for damages a challenger would have 30 days to raise a challenge from the
date they knew or ought to have known about the DoV. This time limit can be extended
by the Courts by up to 3 months where there is ‘good reason’ for doing so. Publishing
notices in the OJEU of the change will assist with an argument that the 30 days runs from
the date of that publication, although this will ultimately be determined by the Court.

For a claim for a declaration of ineffectiveness no challenge could be brought after a date
falling 6 months after the DoV was entered into.

Barclays provide cheque processing services for the out-clearing of Personal and

Why does this contract need to be

What is the reason for the urgency?

In 2015 POL initiated a programme to meet the industry wide HMT and Cheque & Credit
Clearing Company (C&CCC) directive to transition from physical paper to image clearing
in 2017. Subsequently, the industry wide programme suffered significant issues and as
a consequence the full migration from paper to image clearing was delayed to Q4 2019.
We have received an initial recourse of £33k from Barclays for the issues and delays
and they have remediated to point of stability in Q2 2020.

Approval is now sought to extend the services for a further 12 months in order to re-
procure these services during this further 12 month extension to 30 June 2021.

Impact if Exception Declined

Cheque transactions support core services such as mails (stamps and parcels); Bill
Payments (e.g. utilities); and PO Money Savings/ISAs could not be processed, resulting
in cheques not being accepted across our branch counters as payment. This would
impact circa £0.7 billion of our turnover per annum [current annual value of cheque
payments].

RISK & COMPLIANCE COMMITTEE REPORT

Title: Policy Update Meeting Date: I 12 November 2020

What updates were included and why?

2. Asummary that identifies the changes and updates to the policies and statements have
been added below:

Change Management Policy:

In this annual review there were minor updates, this included using the revised template for
the policy to be updated on, along with details of new personnel.
Policy Compliance View

This policy was significantly updated last year. The policy directs clearly what constitutes a
change, how changes should progress through governance and the change principles which
balance these aspects and seek to reduce the risks associated with change.

The Change Excellence Framework SharePoint site provides detailed oversight of all the
processes and controls in place.

The Strategic Portfolio Office also ensures that training is provided for all Heads of
Transformation Portfolio and Change resources, covering any changes to governance
processes. Any new resources are provided with more in-depth training to ensure their
understanding and compliance to the standards.

Conflicts of Interest Policy:
This has had a thorough reviewing covering the below additions:
1.3 - Inclusion of definition of a person connected with a director;

1.6. - Improved detail on directors’ duties under CA 2006 and compliance with the UK Corporate
Governance Code;

2.4 - New reference to the Post Office Conduct Code relating to business standards and greater
detail on the process for reporting.

2.4 - Procurement; new section on managing procurement conflicts, signposting the existing
declaration process.

2.4 — Directors; new section on considerations for directors when identifying and reporting
actual or potential, direct or indirect interests.

Policy Compliance view

A comprehensive update- we have agreed to explore with Co Sec areas to test for control gaps
as part of our second line compliance review.

Protecting Personal Data Policy:

No substantive changes, minor updates to section 1.7 to add Freedom of Information Act, 3.1
to include the eCase tool and 4.3 to refer employees to the Data Protection intranet page for
further help.

Policy Compliance View

Control Standards can be demonstrated as being met; however, these do require the action
and support of Data Owners within the business to ensure these are effective controls. The
working Personal Data Incident, Breach Management and Post Office Individual Rights
Procedures, demonstrate the controls in place and the minimum control standards stated are
being met.

Risk Policy:

The Risk Policy and Risk Appetite Statement are to be covered separately in Mark
Baldock’s risk update paper.

Policy Compliance View

Each minimum control standard stated within the Policy is currently operating. Evidence of each
control is either reflected in the corporate GRC tool or maintained by Central Risk who own the
risk registers, compliance with the policy is demonstrated through the Risk
Registers which provide a detailed oversight of all the processes and controls in place.

Freedom of Information Policy:
This is a new policy that LCG are proposing Post Office adopt.
Policy Compliance View

Given that this is an introduction of a new policy the attestation on the policy performance will
need to be made and carried out next policy annual review.

Assurance

Working with policy owners we are piloting the assurance process and sample testing policies
on a risk basis to review the policy standard and policy compliance.

The Key Policies Intranet Page has now been updated and reflects the following:
e Policy cycle document to show when policies were last reviewed and are due for their
next review;
¢ Policy Approval Form;
« All Group Key Policies.

The page is still work in progress with more content to be added as compliance continue to
develop and build a governance framework around our policies.

POST OFFICE LIMITED
RISK & COMPLIANCE COMMITTEE REPORT

—— Directors & Officers (D&O) : .
Title: Insurarice Renewal Meeting Date: I 12 November 2020
Rutivors Edward Dyer, Working Capital Sponsor Alisdair Cameron, Group Chief
“I and Cash Management Lead i . Finance Officer

Input Sought: Noting

The Committee is asked to note the details of the insurance renewal for 2020/21 and
particularly the Directors & Officers Insurance Renewal..

Executive Summary

Post Office’s insurance cover has been renewed in line with the Audit, Risk & Compliance
Committee (ARC) paper dated 28 October 2020 at a total cost, in line with the estimate
presented, of £2.1m.

Following the ARC approval, the Crime insurance deductible was increased from £2m to £6m
and the corresponding guarantee from NatWest in favour of the Bank of England was raised
accordingly. A breakdown of the insurance premiums is presented in Schedule 1.

Report
D&O Insurance Renewal Challenges

D&O Market Contraction

1. The following factors have driven significant price increases in the D&O insurance market:
. Declining value of insurer investments (insurers invest premiums before having to
pay out for claims);
. Increased claims (Lloyds H1 predicted profits of $1.25bn deteriorated into a $0.5bn
loss. Lloyds ultimately expects to pay Covid-19 claims of over $4bn);
. Lower premium volumes (from reduced economic activity);
. The impact of the virus to the global insurance industry is estimated at over $200bn,
half of which is reduction in insurer investment values; and
. The potential for D&O claims arising out of (Covid-19 related) insolvencies in 2020/21
is of serious concern to insurers.
2. Asa result of these issues, market capacity has reduced, driven by some insurers
exiting D&O insurance and others taking more cautious, reduced positions.
3. Post Office Limited’s (POL) pricing was also impacted by:
. Horizon liabilities; and
. Lack of appetite from some insurers for financial institutions exposure (Lockton
explained to insurers that we are not a bank but provide banking services).
4. Schedule 2 sets out the experience of other corporates. For example, one retailer
experienced a 10x increase in premiums for D&O cover of £40m compared to £60m

Tab 19 Directors & Officers Insurance Renewal

@

the previous year. Lockton noted that those companies with higher D&O insurance
cover than POL’s £60m typically have operations in the USA.

5. POL’s £60m D&O policy has been renewed at a cost of £292,000, a 160% increase on
the 2019/20 premium of £112,500.

Why did the renewal run late?

6. On the 1 November 2020 renewal date, £40m out of the £60m of cover was in place.
By 5 November this was made whole with £20m of additional cover backdated to the
renewal date.

7. The delay was caused by market conditions whereby insurers introduced much more
stringent processes to underwriting risks. Most renewals now require senior
management sign-off and the interrogation of risk has become significantly more
rigorous, resulting in greater work for underwriters and a subsequent slowing of
renewal processes. Further, whilst renewal was initiated earlier than usual, insurers
were unwilling to engage in meaningful discussions until close to renewal, as they
dealt with renewals from the 30 September quarter date.

8. Historically, POL’s insurers have not required updated financials prior to renewal,
accepting receipt of these sometime after renewal. This year, late in the process,
these became a ‘must have’ before some insurers would provide terms. Insurers paid
much closer attention to the regulated and Financial Institutional aspects of the Post
Office business and required a detailed update on the Horizon issues. This arduous
process has not been unique to Post Office, however, and has been a challenge for
brokers and their clients across the market.
